D34 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md Field access uses ., with exactly one elaborated auto-deref through borrow references; -> is rejected.
D35 language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/08-patterns.md, rationale/02-syntax.md Records are nominal named-field product types; construction uses Type { field: expr }, declarations close with build;, and record patterns destructure by field name.
D36/D106/D132 language/03-grammar.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md Indexing uses compiler-known Indexable/IndexableMut; slicing uses checked half-open a[i..j]; both keep total-or-TPOE checked access semantics.
D38/D205/D206 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/08-patterns.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, language/19-examples.md Patterns are nested and exhaustive, use contextual ignore, reject _ and guards, and cannot discard linear payloads or catch-all over possible linear data.
D39 language/03-grammar.md, language/08-patterns.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md while let Pattern := expr do ... od; is refutable-pattern loop sugar that re-evaluates the expression per iteration and breaks on mismatch.
D41 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/18-built-ins.md Bitwise, shift, and rotate operators are keyword operators with explicit grouping, same-type integer operands, and checked count semantics.
D42 language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/16-unsafe-ffi-and-abi.md, language/17-memory-layout-and-backend-contract.md Records have exactly ordinary Kyokai layout, extern record C ABI layout, or packed record byte-tight layout, with layout introspection and packed-field borrow restrictions.
D47/D131 language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/08-patterns.md, language/18-built-ins.md Tuple syntax, tuple types, tuple literals, and tuple destructuring are absent; named records carry multi-value structure.
D48/D162 language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, rationale/05-capabilities.md RootCapability is minted only by runtime bootstrap for entrypoints that request it; safe code cannot acquire root authority later.
D52 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/04-modules-and-visibility.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, language/19-examples.md, rationale/02-syntax.md, appendices/c-austral-differences.md Source files use .kyo interfaces and .kai bodies, and module declarations must match manifest-rooted logical paths.
D53/D140/D142 language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, rationale/03-error-handling-and-tpoe.md Function contracts use require and ensure, are always checked, use ordinary runtime semantics, expose result as a read-only return view, and fail by TPOE.
D54 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/18-built-ins.md Text, raw-string, code-point, and byte literals are distinct literal families.
D55 language/03-grammar.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/18-built-ins.md Array literals use [...], infer only length by counting elements, arrays have Index const length parameters, and array universe classification is Auto.
D56/D57 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md Kyokai has a small precedence table; boolean and/or short-circuit and are the ordinary conditional-evaluation exception.
D58/D191 language/03-grammar.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, language/18-built-ins.md Diverging forms use expression-site Never coercion without general subtyping; potential runtime TPOE is not static divergence.
D59 language/03-grammar.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md Assignment is a sequenced statement, cannot be chained, and produces no value.
D60 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/08-patterns.md Still-live bindings cannot be shadowed, including bindings introduced by patterns.
D62 language/03-grammar.md Module-level mutable var declarations are illegal.
D63 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, rationale/02-syntax.md Comments are //, ///, and //!; block comments and Austral docstrings are rejected.
D65 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/08-patterns.md, language/19-examples.md Union declaration, construction, and pattern forms use multi-field braces, single-field parens, and zero-field bare constructors.
D67 language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, stdlib/08-io-files-env-process-time-random.md, rationale/05-capabilities.md Environment access requires explicit EnvCapability; safe Kyokai has no ambient environment access.
D78/D179/D214 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/04-modules-and-visibility.md, toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Packages, module roots, imports, aliases, selective imports, collisions, file-scope import limits, and module graph construction are specified.
D98 language/03-grammar.md, language/08-patterns.md Record destructuring is total and consumes the record; partial record moves are not part of Kyokai, and linear fields must be bound and consumed.
D88/D235/D252 language/03-grammar.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/15-concurrency.md, language/19-examples.md Spawn syntax uses mandatory capture lists, explicit failure arms, structured taskgroup ... join;, and borrow captures whose lifetime ends at join;.
D108 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md Pipeline |> is rejected; UFCS is the sole built-in left-to-right call-chain surface.
D109/D196 language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/08-patterns.md Single-field records are the nominal wrapper mechanism with one-line declaration syntax, transparent ordinary representation, and named-field destructuring.
D110/D254 language/03-grammar.md, language/04-modules-and-visibility.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md UFCS lookup is ordinary lookup plus a narrow receiver-module fallback resolved during typed elaboration; it is not global method search.
D111/D127 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, rationale/02-syntax.md Borrow scopes close with drop;; foreign blocks close with mon;; borrow scope exits are control-flow boundaries.
D118/D126/D197 language/03-grammar.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md Closure literals have mandatory explicit capture lists, move or borrow their environment visibly, and lower to the callable family selected by strongest access.
D119 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md, rationale/03-error-handling-and-tpoe.md or return err => expr is the explicit error-mapping form and performs no implicit error conversion.
D120 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, stdlib/04-text-bytes-paths-and-strings.md StaticString uses explicit static "..."; ordinary strings are not retargeted by context.
D121/D122/D233/D246 language/03-grammar.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md todo, unreachable, named break/continue, debug purity, and cleanup registration have visible statement syntax plus explicit checker states.
D123 language/03-grammar.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md Body-level target branching is rejected; use whole-file selection, declaration guards, or typeclass abstraction.
D125/D129 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md result and old are contextual contract forms; result is a read-only postcondition view and old snapshots pure entry-state Free expressions.
D135/D261 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md, language/18-built-ins.md Numeric literals use _ separators, modern base prefixes, and a closed suffix set that fixes literal type before context.
D138 language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/08-patterns.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md Record update uses explicit Type { ..., with source }, source-ordered evaluation, and copy/move behavior based on the record universe.
D158/D189 language/03-grammar.md, language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md Generic obligations use bracket parameters plus a closed where clause grammar for typeclass bounds, associated-type bounds, and associated-type equality.
D164/D248 language/03-grammar.md, language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md Spawned tasks are 1:1 OS tasks and task-boundary transfer is explicit through declaration or contract metadata, not Send/Sync inference.
D180 language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md Newlines are insignificant, trailing commas are widely allowed, and empty blocks are no-ops.
D182 language/03-grammar.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md Typeclasses may contain default method bodies, instances may override them, associated types have no defaults, and typeclasses close with spec;.
D187/D238-D240 language/03-grammar.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/08-patterns.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md Borrow/reborrow syntax is checked after explicit elaboration; borrow types are non-owning Free references, mutable-to-immutable use is read reborrow, and inserted borrow/reborrow nodes must pass the conformance matrix.
D190/D192/D193/D195 language/03-grammar.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md Type grammar and semantics stay nominal, rank-1, non-existential, universe-constrained, and exactly-once checked for linear owners.
D198 language/03-grammar.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, stdlib/06-iterators-and-generators.md Generators are named stackless pull iterators with yield, linear suspended state, explicit destroy semantics, and no general coroutine surface.
D242/D242a/D245 language/03-grammar.md, language/04-modules-and-visibility.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/15-concurrency.md, language/16-unsafe-ffi-and-abi.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, stdlib/11-transitional-ffi-tracking.md, rationale/05-capabilities.md, appendices/d-formalization-roadmap.md Unsafe and FFI rules require source-level audit contracts, explicit unsafe authority, safe wrappers through normal visibility, no raw by-value linear or sum-type crossing, and contract-covered ownership/failure/callback behavior.
D255 language/03-grammar.md, language/04-modules-and-visibility.md, language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, stdlib/08-io-files-env-process-time-random.md, rationale/05-capabilities.md Capability declarations are sealed authority types with ordinary ownership rules; unsafe module pragmas and imports do not forge or grant authority.
D33 language/06-type-system.md, language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md, language/08-patterns.md Associated types are the sole instance-determined secondary-type mechanism; projections normalize through selected static instances.
D50 language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md type alias creates transparent synonyms only and introduces no nominal, ABI, or coherence identity.
D61 language/05-declarations.md Foreign integer domains and bitflags use integer aliases plus named constants; closed semantics require wrappers.
D159/D188 language/03-grammar.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md Const generics are explicit Index parameters with deterministic compile-time value equality and exact admitted argument forms.
D160/D217 language/06-type-system.md Recursive nominal types are legal only when the fully expanded layout graph has finite size through explicit indirection-bearing fields.
D176 language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md, stdlib/05-collections.md, rationale/01-language-design.md Kyokai has no general Cloneable; deep duplication remains explicit, type-specific, and allocator-visible when allocation occurs.
D177 language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md, stdlib/05-collections.md, rationale/01-language-design.md Kyokai has no general Default; generic code cannot fabricate values from nothing or assume zero-bit construction.
D181 language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md Phantom parameters are legal and affect identity/coherence, while zero-field user records and general ZST marker culture are rejected.
D186 language/06-type-system.md Kyokai has no general variance system; user generics are invariant and Never lifting is closed to built-in Optional/Result.
D194 language/05-declarations.md, language/06-type-system.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, rationale/04-linear-resources.md Universe classification is explicit per constructor; generic Auto becomes linear iff a type argument is linear, unless the constructor has a special closed rule.
D209/D161 language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md, language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md Call-site generic type argument inference is argument-driven, forward-only, local, and never solved from return or target context.
D215 language/05-declarations.md Module constants are lazy, cached, cycle-checked across modules, and have no semantic order unless dependency forces one.
D216 language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md Generic instance overlap diagnostics must name conflicting instances and include a concrete witness substitution when possible.
D2a/D2b/D207 language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, language/15-concurrency.md Deferred actions run per lexical scope in LIFO order, eligible by explicit exit category; panic runs ordinary defer, TPOE does not, and deferred bodies cannot redirect the outer control-flow path.
D23 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md, language/18-built-ins.md Operator overloading exists only through fixed built-in operator typeclasses with static coherent dispatch and no user-defined operators.
D37/D210 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md Numeric conversion uses explicit UFCS-style conversion names; Index is a distinct integer domain and never ambiently interchangeable.
D40/D40a/D102 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, stdlib/02-core-result-optional-display-error.md, rationale/03-error-handling-and-tpoe.md Formatting uses Displayable/FormatSink; format is allocator-explicit and fallible, writeFmt is non-allocating stream output, and debug observes through formatting only in debug/test instrumentation.
D44 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, stdlib/03-allocators-and-memory-containers.md, rationale/03-error-handling-and-tpoe.md, rationale/07-stdlib-philosophy.md Allocator choice is explicit at fresh-allocation boundaries; there is no hidden default allocator and containers store allocator identity when their contract says so.
D250-D251 language/17-memory-layout-and-backend-contract.md, language/18-built-ins.md, language/19-examples.md, stdlib/03-allocators-and-memory-containers.md Kyokai rejects ambient, thread-local, or default allocator strategy; explicit runtime allocator handles remain the source-level model.
D43/D128 language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md Loops are statements, break carries no value, and search ergonomics use ordinary iterator helpers rather than loop expressions.
D46 language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md Immutable let := may omit a type only when the initializer already has one fully determined denotable type.
D71 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md Expression and statement subparts evaluate strictly left-to-right, with short-circuit Boolean operators as the ordinary conditional-evaluation exception.
D72/D213 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md Temporaries live for the statement; immutable rvalue borrows may not escape, mutable rvalue borrows are illegal, and mutating UFCS on rvalue temporaries is rejected.
D73 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/12-implicit-completions-and-elaboration.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, language/15-concurrency.md, language/16-unsafe-ffi-and-abi.md, language/17-memory-layout-and-backend-contract.md, rationale/01-language-design.md, appendices/d-formalization-roadmap.md Accepted Kyokai operations have specified outcomes; unsafe primitives are individually specified; expression failures, unreachable, fatal paths, raw memory boundaries, and safe concurrency behavior are not backend undefined behavior.
D75/D76 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, language/18-built-ins.md, stdlib/07-math-and-numerics.md, rationale/03-error-handling-and-tpoe.md Integer arithmetic is same-type and checked-by-default with TPOE on specified traps; contract arithmetic uses the same rules, and floating arithmetic follows the strict IEEE 754 contract.
D77 language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, stdlib/03-allocators-and-memory-containers.md, stdlib/05-collections.md, stdlib/06-iterators-and-generators.md, rationale/04-linear-resources.md, rationale/07-stdlib-philosophy.md Safe container APIs tie element and iterator borrows to container regions; mutation that could invalidate live borrows is rejected or specified per container contract.
D84/D253 language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md, language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, language/15-concurrency.md, rationale/01-language-design.md, rationale/03-error-handling-and-tpoe.md Ordinary completion, panic, TPOE, and runtime-fatal termination are distinct; Kyokai has no in-process catch for panic or TPOE, including across task joins.
D94/D257 language/16-unsafe-ffi-and-abi.md, language/17-memory-layout-and-backend-contract.md Volatile/MMIO access is unsafe operation-level readVolatile/writeVolatile, not synchronization and not a reference/type qualifier.
D89/D199 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, language/17-memory-layout-and-backend-contract.md, rationale/04-linear-resources.md Moves have as-if bytewise relocation semantics, moved-from places become unusable, self-reference requires stable-address rules, and large return values use guaranteed direct result placement without creating a stable-address guarantee.
D89a/D89b language/06-type-system.md, language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, rationale/04-linear-resources.md Safe self-reference requires a stable-address boundary; pinned types and PinBox[T] are the admitted non-movable model, and generic relocation must require Movable.
D202/D203 language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md Compile-time evaluation uses deterministic step budgets and scratch memory that is not a language-visible allocator.
D90/D90a/D247 language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md, appendices/d-formalization-roadmap.md Cross-task ordering is a closed happens-before model over spawn/join, channel transfer/closure, atomics, and fences; relaxed operations do not synchronize by themselves.
D91/D237 language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/08-io-files-env-process-time-random.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md Cancellation is cooperative; plain blocking operations may wait indefinitely, while deadline/cancellation-aware operations use explicit readiness paths and result cases.
D92/D258 language/03-grammar.md, language/15-concurrency.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md Multi-channel waiting uses select ... when ... do ... pick; with one selected ready arm and no source-order priority guarantee.
D93/D234 language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md Poller is explicit linear readiness state; event loops are ordinary Kyokai code over pollers, not hidden runtime services.
D95/D256 language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/08-io-files-env-process-time-random.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md Safe signal handling is capability-gated, notification-based, pollable through SignalWatcher, and synchronous fault signals are runtime-fatal.
D100/D184 language/15-concurrency.md, language/18-built-ins.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md Mutex[T] and RwLock[T] are linear synchronization primitives with linear guards; concurrency guidance prefers channels first, locks second, atomics last.
D101 language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md Reference-counted shared ownership through Rc[T] or Arc[T] is rejected; sharing uses ownership transfer, structured borrows, synchronization, arenas, or indices.
D113a/D113b language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/16-unsafe-ffi-and-abi.md, stdlib/11-transitional-ffi-tracking.md Raw dynamic loading is unsafe, capability-gated, and represented by linear handles; safe plugins use verified Kyokai plugin contracts and explicit init/shutdown.
D141 language/15-concurrency.md, language/18-built-ins.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md The C backend lowers Atomic[T] through C11 atomics and rejects toolchains that cannot preserve required atomic semantics.
D27 language/17-memory-layout-and-backend-contract.md, toolchain/04-build-profiles-targets-linking.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Debug/source mapping is profile-controlled, path-remapped for reproducibility, and exposed through backend/playground artifact modes while preserving C #line or target-equivalent metadata as required.
D146 language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/06-iterators-and-generators.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md, rationale/07-stdlib-philosophy.md Receiver[T: Linear] completes through explicit drain; only Receiver[T: Free] may close and discard buffered values.
D156 language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/06-iterators-and-generators.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md Kyokai has no language-level async/await/futures/executors; high-concurrency I/O uses explicit Poller-based libraries.
D168 language/15-concurrency.md Child-task result/error communication uses explicit channels or synchronization; panic and TPOE are not task result values.
D183 language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md, rationale/06-concurrency.md Rendezvous channels use explicit construction and synchronous handoff; bounded channels require capacity at least one.
D212/D236 language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/08-io-files-env-process-time-random.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md Raw capability-bearing I/O is exclusive by handle; multi-task sharing uses explicit brokers or explicit synchronized wrappers, not hidden runtime mutexes.
D235 language/15-concurrency.md Thread creation failure is explicit ThreadSpawnError at spawn or covered by pre-reserved task capacity; failed spawn transfers no captures.
D262 language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, rationale/01-language-design.md, rationale/03-error-handling-and-tpoe.md Stack overflow is runtime-fatal and must be detected or guarded before safe Kyokai memory invariants can be corrupted.
Austral goals language/01-goals-and-non-goals.md, rationale/01-language-design.md, appendices/c-austral-differences.md Compatible inherited goals are carried into Kyokai directly: simplicity, correctness, security, readability, maintainability, modularity, strictness, and restraint.
Attribution policy language/00-introduction.md, language/01-goals-and-non-goals.md, rationale/00-rationale-index.md, appendices/a-license.md, appendices/c-austral-differences.md Wording from Fernando Borretti’s Austral specification is marked as source text from Austral; Kyokai authorship is not attributed to Borretti; internal writing guides are not public trace sources.
Rationale policy rationale/00-rationale-index.md Rationale chapters are non-normative explanation, credit Borretti’s Austral source wording when used, and defer exact behavior to normative language, toolchain, stdlib, and appendix chapters.
Austral difference index appendices/c-austral-differences.md Kyokai indexes inherited Austral files, replacement homes, and retirement status while keeping the Kyokai spec self-contained.
D25 toolchain/06-formatter.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md kyokai fmt is deterministic, idempotent, zero-config, edition-aware, parse-preserving, and does not perform semantic rewrites.
D26 toolchain/00-toolchain-overview.md, toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, toolchain/03-cli.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md The single kyokai binary uses shared manifest/workspace scope, stable commands, explicit profile/target/backend selection, stable streams, and stable exit behavior.
D28 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/07-testing-coverage-bench.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Inline tests, doc tests, coverage, and benchmarks run through ordinary compiler semantics and explicit harness modes.
D29 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/05-diagnostics.md, toolchain/07-testing-coverage-bench.md, toolchain/08-docs-lsp-audit.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Diagnostics have stable codes, severity, spans, JSON records, suggestions, suppression policy, deterministic ordering, and command/runner failure categories.
D31 toolchain/04-build-profiles-targets-linking.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md Build profiles, target/backend tool configuration, output types, link mode, native dependencies, and release artifacts are explicit configuration.
D51 toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Dependencies are workspace package references or pinned Git revisions; tags are checked labels, branches are rejected, caches verify revisions, and index discovery does not replace pins.
D79 language/04-modules-and-visibility.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, toolchain/08-docs-lsp-audit.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md .koi is a versioned package interface contract artifact used for dependency checking, docs, LSP, audit, reproducibility, compatibility, and concrete KBI artifact exchange.
D80 toolchain/04-build-profiles-targets-linking.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md Target triples are legal only by explicit target matrix/spec, have support tiers, and reject unsupported backend/target combinations early.
D83 toolchain/00-toolchain-overview.md, toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, toolchain/04-build-profiles-targets-linking.md, toolchain/06-formatter.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Build identity, lockfiles, caches, paths, generated sources, artifacts, release provenance, and package resolution are reproducible by default.
D105 toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, toolchain/06-formatter.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Package manifests select language edition; tools parse/check/format source by edition; .koi compatibility requires exact edition match; editions are not SemVer.
D137 toolchain/07-testing-coverage-bench.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md Tests, eval, generators, and playground execution receive no ambient authority; capability-using code declares its authority and gets isolated capability instances where applicable.
D144 toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Incremental compilation is a package/module/query optimization with exact fingerprint invalidation and no semantic effect.
D148 toolchain/08-docs-lsp-audit.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md kyokai lsp is the official language server and shares the compiler engine, diagnostics, manifest model, and semantic checks.
D149 toolchain/04-build-profiles-targets-linking.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md Cross-compilation uses manifest-centered target tables, importable target-spec TOML, backend-specific tool config, and reproducible target-spec inputs.
D150 toolchain/08-docs-lsp-audit.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md, rationale/05-capabilities.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md kyokai audit reports dependency, unsafe, FFI, capability, native, generation, reproducibility, and API risk facts without changing semantics.
D151/D151a toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md kyokai eval and kyokai repl use the real compiler engine; REPL sessions are persistent and obey linear cleanup on reset/quit.
D157 toolchain/00-toolchain-overview.md, toolchain/05-diagnostics.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Toolchain releases classify compatibility impact, use a later four-week train, and keep editions separate from ordinary releases.
D200 toolchain/04-build-profiles-targets-linking.md Identical-code folding is profile-controlled and allowed only when observable Kyokai behavior, debug needs, exported symbols, and provenance remain valid.
D218 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/07-testing-coverage-bench.md, toolchain/08-docs-lsp-audit.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md kyokai doc produces public-interface HTML/JSON, renders contracts, extracts explicit doc tests, and supplies SemVer/audit metadata.
D221 toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md The official package index is a read-only discovery index and does not replace pinned source revisions.
D223 toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Package SemVer is an advisory API/version convention checked against public interfaces and .koi metadata, while lockfiles remain revision-based.
D225 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/05-diagnostics.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Official CI and release artifacts include setup support, OCI images, checksums, provenance, stable diagnostics, and portable install behavior.
D226 toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md Compiler Explorer and sandbox-runner behavior are official toolchain contracts; a hosted playground is optional.
D243 toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md Mixed-edition workspaces are structurally legal, .koi consumption requires exact edition compatibility, and stdlib/package evolution uses SemVer where source semantics are not changing.
D244 toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md Package yanks are append-only metadata that block new selection while preserving existing lockfile meaning unless policy rejects them.
D264 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/04-build-profiles-targets-linking.md, toolchain/09-reproducibility-incremental-builds.md, toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Build outputs use kyokai-out/, disposable tool state uses .kyokai-cache/, artifacts are partitioned by target/profile/backend/package, and clean/override behavior is explicit.
D265 toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md, toolchain/03-cli.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md .koi uses the canonical KBI-1 binary container with required sections, exact compatibility fields, canonical hashing, and official verify/print/diff commands.
D266 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/01-manifest-package-workspace.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md kyokai init and kyokai new create deterministic project templates with explicit manifests, module roots, and non-destructive behavior.
D267 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/05-diagnostics.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Diagnostic explanations are shipped locally through kyokai explain; kyokai fix applies only validated machine-applicable suggestions by default.
D268 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md kyokai --version and kyokai doctor expose toolchain identity, host setup, backend/target support, and common setup failures without requiring a project.
D269 toolchain/03-cli.md, toolchain/10-package-index-semver-releases-ci.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Package remove/search/info/tree/why/outdated/vendor workflows are specified as read-only inspection or explicit pinned offline materialization commands.
D270 toolchain/07-testing-coverage-bench.md, rationale/08-toolchain-philosophy.md Property and fuzz testing include seed, replay, corpus, minimization, list, and failed-test rerun controls with reproducible report artifacts.
D82/D82a/D82b language/07-generics-and-typeclasses.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md Generics and typeclasses dispatch statically without hidden runtime dictionaries; .koi metadata must support downstream checking and materialization.

Austral Difference Index

[Rikona Kurasaki / Mjoyufull] Kyokai is a fork, not a denial. Austral remains the source of many good bones: linear types, capability direction, explicit modules, strictness, and a readable spec tradition. This appendix maps where Kyokai carries Austral ideas forward, where it changes them, and where Borretti’s Austral wording is credited as source material instead of being presented as Kyokai authorship.

Trace: D5, D86, Attribution policy Covers: Kyokai is self-contained while preserving traceable Austral lineage and attribution.

Difference Families

Family Kyokai Direction Normative Home Trace
Project identity Kyokai uses Kyokai.*, .kyo, .kai, Kyokai package manifests, and Kyokai-owned terminology. language/00-introduction.md, language/04-modules-and-visibility.md, toolchain/02-module-resolution-and-koi.md D1, D5, D52, D78
Spec shape Kyokai has language, toolchain, stdlib, rationale, and appendix families instead of one inherited language-only document. language/00-introduction.md, toolchain/00-toolchain-overview.md, stdlib/00-stdlib-overview.md D86, D152, D229
Syntax Kyokai changes terminators, borrow spelling, pattern forms, fallible control flow, generics, records, modules, and comments. language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md D7b-D19a, D35-D43, D52, D63
Error model Kyokai splits Result, Optional, panic, TPOE, runtime-fatal, allocation failure, and StandardError. language/13-contracts-and-runtime-failure.md, stdlib/02-core-result-optional-display-error.md D24, D53, D74, D84, D253, D259
Ownership/borrows Kyokai keeps linear ownership but specifies regions, moves, invalidation, pinning, deferred cleanup, and elaboration. language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md D6, D77, D89, D89a-D89b, D187, D238-D240
Capabilities Kyokai keeps capability security and expands sealed declarations, root authority, stdlib authority APIs, audit, and task transfer. language/14-capabilities-and-authority.md, stdlib/08-io-files-env-process-time-random.md D48, D67, D171, D211-D212, D255
Concurrency Kyokai adds structured tasks, SPSC channels, select, pollers, locks, atomics, cancellation, and signal handling. language/15-concurrency.md, stdlib/09-concurrency-primitives.md D3, D90-D101, D146, D183-D184, D256
Unsafe/FFI/backend Kyokai specifies unsafe contracts, C ABI, dynamic loading, generated-C safety, LLVM path, volatile/MMIO, and no language UB. language/16-unsafe-ffi-and-abi.md, language/17-memory-layout-and-backend-contract.md D20, D73, D113a-D113b, D139, D228, D245
Standard library Kyokai replaces inherited stdlib assumptions with admitted Kyokai.* API families and explicit contracts. stdlib/00-stdlib-overview.md through stdlib/11-transitional-ffi-tracking.md D64, D85, D152, D229-D232
Toolchain Kyokai specifies CLI, manifests, packages, .koi, formatter, tests, docs, LSP, audit, reproducibility, releases, and output/cache layout. toolchain/00-toolchain-overview.md through toolchain/11-build-generation-and-playground.md D25-D31, D51, D78-D80, D83, D218, D264-D265

Trace: D5, D86, D152, D229 Covers: Differences are indexed by family and point to normative Kyokai chapters.

Austral Source Replacement Map

The old inherited Austral chapter files are out of the active Kyokai build after replacement by Kyokai chapters. They remain important source history in git and in Borretti’s Austral project, but the reader should use the Kyokai chapters below for current behavior. src/appendix-a.md is different: it carries the full GFDL text included with the built specification.

Austral Source Area Kyokai Replacement / Status
Introduction language/00-introduction.md and rationale chapters.

Syntax language/02-lexical-syntax.md, language/03-grammar.md, rationale/02-syntax.md.

Declarations language/05-declarations.md.
Statements language/10-statements-and-control-flow.md.
Expressions language/09-expressions-and-evaluation.md.
Linearity language/11-linearity-borrowing-and-regions.md, rationale/04-linear-resources.md.
Built-ins and pervasive APIs language/18-built-ins.md and stdlib chapters.
Memory support Memory/layout/backend and allocator stdlib chapters.
FFI language/16-unsafe-ffi-and-abi.md, stdlib/11-transitional-ffi-tracking.md.
Examples and style language/19-examples.md, syntax/naming rules, and future style guidance.

Full GFDL text src/appendix-a.md, navigated by appendices/a-license.md.

Trace: D5, D86, Attribution policy Covers: Old Austral chapter files have Kyokai replacements, Borretti source wording is credited when used, and the GFDL text remains included.

Reader Rule

If a new Kyokai chapter and an inherited Austral file overlap, read the Kyokai chapter as the current normative home. If Borretti’s Austral wording is worth using, put it in the Kyokai chapter or rationale with a source note instead of making the reader reconcile two documents.

Trace: D5, D86, D155 Covers: The Kyokai spec is self-contained and inherited files do not override extracted Kyokai chapters.

Formalization Roadmap

[Rikona Kurasaki / Mjoyufull] This appendix records the proof road. It does not pretend the proof is already done. Kyokai’s prose can state the language contract, but the sequential ownership core still needs the paper theorem before v1.0 and later mechanization after self-hosting.

Trace: D143/D241 Covers: Kyokai requires a paper proof for the sequential core before v1.0 and later mechanized proof work.

Proof Scope

The first calculus is lambda_K-seq: a small sequential core for ownership, borrowing, moves, regions, linear consumption, pattern binding, control-flow joins, checked failure, and TPOE. It deliberately excludes concurrency, FFI, backend lowering, package resolution, the full stdlib, and toolchain behavior.

Trace: D143/D241, D90, D245 Covers: The first formalization is sequential and excludes concurrency, FFI, backend, and stdlib/toolchain layers.

Required Paper Artifact

The paper proof must define abstract syntax, typing judgments, store/ownership state, borrow-region state, small-step operational semantics, checked failure/TPOE outcomes, progress, preservation, and the exact theorem statement for the safe sequential core. Any gap must be named as an assumption or excluded feature.

Trace: D73, D143/D241 Covers: The paper proof must specify syntax, typing, semantics, failure outcomes, and soundness theorem scope.

Milestones

Milestone Output Status Meaning
Scope freeze Feature list for lambda_K-seq with exclusions. The calculus knows what it is proving.
Core syntax Abstract syntax for expressions, statements, owners, borrows, regions, and failure forms. Surface syntax is not required; elaborated core is enough.
Static judgments Typing, ownership, borrowing, movement, region, and control-flow join judgments. The checker rules have a proof-facing shape.
Dynamic semantics Small-step semantics with store, ownership state, and named failure outcomes. Evaluation behavior is explicit.
Soundness theorem Progress/preservation adapted to linear ownership and TPOE. The theorem says what cannot go wrong and what may terminate.
Paper proof Human-checkable proof document. Required before v1.0.
Mechanized plan Proof assistant selection and encoding strategy. Planned after self-hosting; Coq is the current likely first target.

Trace: D143/D241 Covers: Formalization work proceeds through explicit artifacts instead of vague proof intent.

Relation To Existing Notes

kyokailang/kyokaicalculus/lambda_k_research.md is the current research note and scope map. It is not itself the normative proof. When a proof artifact is produced, this appendix must point to the theorem, proof document, assumptions, and excluded features.

Trace: D143/D241 Covers: The research note informs proof work but does not replace the required proof artifact.

Later Extensions

After the sequential proof, later formalization work can add concurrency happens-before reasoning, task transfer, channels, cancellation, unsafe/FFI contracts, backend lowering preservation, stdlib contract models, and mechanized proof. These layers should not be started by blurring the first theorem; they should extend it after the core is stable.

Trace: D90-D101, D143/D241, D228, D245 Covers: Concurrency, unsafe/FFI, backend, and stdlib proof work are later extensions.

Proof Honesty Rule

Until a theorem is actually discharged, spec text may say language contract, design goal, or intended invariant. It must not claim a mechanized or paper proof exists. When the proof changes a rule, the normative chapter and traceability appendix must be updated in the same pass.

Trace: D143/D241, D155 Covers: The spec must not overclaim proof status and must keep proof-driven rule changes traceable.

If the Document does not specify a version number of this License, you may choose any version ever published (not as a draft) by the Free Software Foundation. If the Document specifies that a proxy can decide which future versions of this License can be used, that proxy’s public statement of acceptance of a version permanently authorizes you to choose that version for the Document.

11. RELICENSING

“Massive Multiauthor Collaboration Site” (or “MMC Site”) means any World Wide Web server that publishes copyrightable works and also provides prominent facilities for anybody to edit those works. A public wiki that anybody can edit is an example of such a server. A “Massive Multiauthor Collaboration” (or “MMC”) contained in the site means any set of copyrightable works thus published on the MMC site.

“CC-BY-SA” means the Creative Commons Attribution-Share Alike 3.0 license published by Creative Commons Corporation, a not-for-profit corporation with a principal place of business in San Francisco, California, as well as future copyleft versions of that license published by that same organization.

“Incorporate” means to publish or republish a Document, in whole or in part, as part of another Document.

An MMC is “eligible for relicensing” if it is licensed under this License, and if all works that were first published under this License somewhere other than this MMC, and subsequently incorporated in whole or in part into the MMC, (1) had no cover texts or invariant sections, and (2) were thus incorporated prior to November 1, 2008.

The operator of an MMC Site may republish an MMC contained in the site under CC-BY-SA on the same site at any time before August 1, 2009, provided the MMC is eligible for relicensing.

ADDENDUM: How to use this License for your documents

To use this License in a document you have written, include a copy of the License in the document and put the following copyright and license notices just after the title page:

    Copyright (C)  YEAR  YOUR NAME.
    Permission is granted to copy, distribute and/or modify this document
    under the terms of the GNU Free Documentation License, Version 1.3
    or any later version published by the Free Software Foundation;
    with no Invariant Sections, no Front-Cover Texts, and no Back-Cover Texts.
    A copy of the license is included in the section entitled "GNU
    Free Documentation License".

If you have Invariant Sections, Front-Cover Texts and Back-Cover Texts, replace the “with … Texts.” line with this:

    with the Invariant Sections being LIST THEIR TITLES, with the
    Front-Cover Texts being LIST, and with the Back-Cover Texts being LIST.

If you have Invariant Sections without Cover Texts, or some other combination of the three, merge those two alternatives to suit the situation.

If your document contains nontrivial examples of program code, we recommend releasing these examples in parallel under your choice of free software license, such as the GNU General Public License, to permit their use in free software.
